Jiang Customs Explains the Scope of Application of Import Tariff No. 589 95

The Jiang Customs issued a joint notice No. 1550 to explain the scope of application of import tariff No. 589, stating, "According to the order of the Ministry of Finance, it is now determined that starting from October 16 this year, the scope of application of item 589 of the Import Tariff of the Customs of the Republic of China is limited to teak (beams, planks, sections) with a value of more than 30 gold units per cubic meter. Teak (beams, planks, sections) with lower values shall be classified under item 590 of the tariff, unspecified timber, and taxed at 20% ad valorem." This is to be followed. All merchants are hereby informed. Supervisor Zhu Changnian, Tax Officer Baron Shen.

Notice from the Electrical Silk Weaving Industry: Stamp the Ends of the Bolt of Fabric to Protect Legitimate Goods and Assist in Anti-Smuggling; The Deadline for Stamping is the End of this Month 96

According to the Datong News Agency, the Electrical Silk Weaving Industry Association issued a notice stating that in order to assist the government in anti-smuggling and protect the transportation and sale of legitimate goods, the association will conduct an appraisal of silk fabrics produced by members starting from October 1. The ends of the silk bolts will be stamped to identify them. The association has previously notified all member factories to comply with this. Now, the association will implement the appraisal procedure for both old and new goods produced by members. In addition to having the executive and supervisory committee members supervise the stamping of old goods, specialists will be assigned to various major refining factories to stamp the fabrics daily at a specified time in order to complete the process in the shortest possible time, so that domestically produced legitimate silk fabrics can have convenient transportation and sales opportunities. The association also convened a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees on the 12th of this month and decided to stamp the products and notify members to comply quickly. Those who have not applied for appraisal must fill out the application form immediately and apply to the association. If the application procedure has been completed, but the refining factory that is undertaking the refining of the products does not have a stamping agent stationed by the association, the refining factory should be notified to send the refined goods to the association for stamping in the same amount every day. Do not neglect this, as it will hinder the transportation and sale of the products. The association has now stipulated that the stamping of both old and new goods must be completed by October 31 in accordance with the specified procedures. Starting from November 1, if any member's products are found to be unstamped, the association will no longer provide certification. If any problems arise in the future when unstamped silk fabrics are transported and sold to various parts of the country, the association will not be able to handle them. This has been unanimously approved and recorded. In addition to sending separate letters, this is also announced in the newspaper. It is hoped that all member factories will apply for appraisal and stamping before October 31. This is very important.

Torrent of Goods Heading Up the Yangtze River Creates Record High, Worth 30 to 40 Million Yuan This Month Alone 99

Since autumn this year, the volume of goods shipped from Shanghai along the Yangtze River has been unprecedented since 1935. The situation has become particularly congested since the first of this month. In just over twenty days, the goods shipped from Shanghai to various ports along the Yangtze River, based on October statistics, have filled approximately seventy ships traveling to the Yangtze (including the middle and upper reaches of the Yangtze). Almost every one of these seventy Yangtze River boats was fully loaded when departing Shanghai, with ten out of ten compartments filled with cargo. As early as the 27th and 28th of last month, congestion was already apparent, but after the first of this month, Yangtze River merchants purchased goods in even greater quantities, loading them immediately upon acquisition, without any delay. Goods previously purchased and stored in Shanghai warehouses were also moved out at this time. The tonnage requirements of various merchant houses needing space on ships have exhausted the capacity of the six major shipping companies, leading to a situation of too many goods and too few ships, resulting in a severe shortage of tonnage, an unprecedented situation for Yangtze River shipping since 1935. The business revenue and freight volume of the six companies are also increasing daily. Company executives are visibly pleased. According to investigations, in just over twenty days, goods worth at least 30 million yuan have been shipped from Shanghai to the provinces of Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan, exceeding one million dan (a unit of weight) in total. A large quantity of goods still awaits shipment in Shanghai warehouses, including 200,000 bags of white sugar alone, which cannot be shipped due to lack of tonnage. Additionally, over 10,000 tons of timber are urgently awaiting shipment. Cotton yarn, driven by rising prices, has already been prioritized for export. Current surveys indicate that Shanghai is experiencing a shortage of cotton yarn. Piece goods are still being loaded, and the demand for hardware products shipped upstream is also very high. The reporter, seeking to understand why Yangtze River exports this year (especially this month) are so congested, conducted a special investigation. According to Yangtze River merchants, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan have all experienced bumper harvests this year, resulting in strong purchasing power among the people, so the demand for daily necessities has increased several times compared to previous years. The large-scale purchases and transportation of sugar, seafood, hardware, foreign cloth, cotton yarn, timber, etc., to the Yangtze River are partly for stockpiling and partly for construction purposes. This is a special circumstance. Some are even building new houses in the upper Yangtze region specifically for use as storage warehouses. Furthermore, many new shops have recently opened in Changsha, Hankou, and Shashi due to the economic recovery of farmers. Another reason is that the Yangtze River water level has receded earlier this year. Currently, the lowest point in the upper reaches still has seventeen feet of water, while the lowest point in the lower reaches only has fourteen to fifteen feet. If it does not rain for a long time, the outflow from the upper Yangtze will decrease, and there is concern that the Yangtze River will dry up completely during the winter dry season. Therefore, shipping companies are raising water level fees early, and merchants are also stocking up on winter goods early to prevent difficulties navigating during the dry season. This is also a major factor contributing to the booming business.

Raw Silk Sales Improve, September Exports Reach 1,500 Bales, Further Increases Expected 100

According to the Shin Shi News Agency, raw silk sales have recently improved. The reporter's inquiries with silk industry sources indicate that the reasons for the improved exports are: the ongoing Spanish Civil War and a clear international backdrop signaling that a second World War is imminent. Although the devaluation of the French franc is unfavorable for trade with the Gold Bloc countries, the need for European and American countries to stockpile raw materials for wartime purposes has led to large-scale purchases by France, the United States, Britain, and Germany. Moreover, the impact of the devaluation and financial crisis that has happened to countries that used to be a part of the Gold Bloc on the international market, specifically the Japanese export to France, Switzerland, and Italy, is greater than it is for China, so the devaluation of the French franc will only raise the price of Chinese silk. Sales will not suffer a great blow. It is reported that raw silk exports in September reached approximately 1,500 bales, double the 700 bales in August. The situation has improved further this month. It is expected that raw silk exports will increase further amidst the turmoil in Europe.

Seamen's Union Warns Shipmates to Pay Attention to Six Points 102

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Seamen's Union has always been serious about implementing the New Life Movement among shipmates. It has now issued a circular warning shipmates not to smoke opium, carry contraband, bring illegal items, insult passengers, or extort tips. The text of the circular is as follows: "Smoking opium and carrying contraband are strictly prohibited by law. The union has repeatedly issued orders to strictly prohibit these actions. Since the issuance of these orders, many have complied, but a few who disregard the law continue to engage in these activities secretly. Recently, some shipmates in the middle class have been disrespectful to passengers during work hours, even extorting tips and disobeying the captain's orders. Such behavior damages the reputation of our seamen and must be strictly prohibited. Here are the points to pay attention to: (1) Do not smoke opium or other drugs. (2) Do not carry contraband or illegal items. (3) Do not insult passengers or extort tips. (4) Do not disobey the orders of the captain or purser. (5) If a ship incident occurs, make every effort to rescue others. (6) Do not violate the union's regulations. Any member of the union who violates any of the above rules after the issuance of this circular will be severely punished without leniency. All are to comply with this order."

To Avoid Japanese Misunderstandings, Police Use Written Language Instead of Speech, Using Japanese Slips of Paper to Communicate with Japanese in Cases of Language Barriers 104

According to the French newspaper translated by the Foreign News Agency, since the Japanese sailor incident on Hai'ning Road, disputes have frequently occurred between Japanese residents and Chinese citizens in this city. The Public Security Bureau believes that a major cause of these incidents is language barriers. As a result of research, a preventive measure has been developed: using a small printed slip of paper to replace speech, to avoid misunderstandings. Starting from the 25th, police officers at the North Station branch and other locations have been equipped with these printed slips of paper, containing the following eight items: 1. Where are you going? Please write it down and show me. 2. Please do not go to that remote area. 3. I am now escorting you to the police station to talk with someone who understands Japanese. 4. Do you have a business card? Please give me one. 5. Please wait here for a moment while I get someone who understands Japanese to come. 6. I am calling someone who understands Japanese to talk with you. 7. Please tell me your nationality, name, and address. 8. Your actions may cause misunderstandings among the people. I am taking you to the police station to talk with someone who understands Japanese. These printed slips of paper are in Japanese on one side and Chinese on the other. If an incident occurs and there is a language barrier, the police can immediately show the Japanese person the Japanese slip of paper, asking them to go to the police station or asking where they are going.

Anhui and Shaanxi Report on Disaster Conditions 109

Taihe Drought Disaster: The United Southeast China General Office of the World Red Swastika Society received a report yesterday from the Taihe branch in Anhui Province on the severe drought conditions and the urgent need for relief. Letters have been sent to various branches to appeal for assistance. The original letter is reproduced below: (Omitted Titles) "Taihe is a land of poor soil and impoverished people. In years of good harvest, the yields are barely sufficient. In years of crop failure, starvation is inevitable. Last year's autumn drought was disastrous, with no harvest of soybeans, buckwheat, or mung beans. The cries of hunger are everywhere, a scene too terrible to witness. Our society and other charitable organizations raised funds for relief, which, while not without some benefit, was merely a drop in the bucket. A second appeal for spring relief went unanswered. When the winter wheat was about to ripen, the refugees gradually returned. However, since the latter part of May and throughout June and July, not a drop of rain has fallen. Seven or eight out of ten fields of soybeans, sweet potatoes, and other miscellaneous grains have not been planted. Those that have been planted have been scorched and withered, even worse than last autumn. The days ahead are long and hopeless. Thousands of families are fleeing to other places, taking the old and supporting the young. What will become of them when the severe winter arrives? Therefore, we publicly implore you to show your divine benevolence and urgently allocate relief funds to provide assistance. The disaster victims of the entire county will be eternally grateful and will never forget your kindness. We weep with tears and await your urgent response."

Shaanxi Bandit Disaster: Northern Shaanxi has been occupied by bandits for years. After repeated campaigns by the National Army, the area has been gradually pacified. The affected people in the recovered areas are unable to survive. The Executive Yuan has now allocated 300,000 yuan and dispatched He Shaonan, a member of the Relief Committee, to lead relief workers with funds to provide assistance. The Relief Committee has received a letter from Qiu Xiang, the relief commissioner of Luochuan, from Suide, describing the disaster conditions. The letter is reproduced below: "To your excellency, I sent an airmail letter from Xi'an, hoping you have seen it. I followed Commissioner He with seven relief workers, borrowing Deputy Commander Zhang's plane to fly to Suide. I have had brief conversations with Commander Tang and Division Commander Gao, and learned about the situation in northern Shaanxi. Except for Luochuan and five or six other counties where transportation is relatively convenient, the rest face great transportation difficulties. Food is completely lacking. Yanchuan County was recently recovered. There are only about one hundred households in the city. In the countryside, there are two villages, each with about three or four hundred households, totaling only about a thousand households. The situation in the villages near the bandit areas and the newly recovered cities is roughly the same. Counties not affected by bandits have a very large population, such as Suide County, which has more than 120,000 people. The current relief funds cannot be allocated without on-site surveys. Li Yuhai and Xi Chaofan have been sent to the first and second relief districts to conduct surveys. The fifth district is completely inaccessible. Since the bandit disasters, people in all counties have gathered together. One can travel for dozens of miles before seeing a village. Livestock has also decreased. The daily price of a donkey is at least one or two yuan. Relief workers have no choice but to walk. We will do our best to live up to your expectations. The survey personnel in the first and second relief districts will not be able to reach Suide until ten days later. The survey will begin in half a month. I will report on the progress later. Qiu Xiang, October 12."

Launching a fund-raising association. The inspection of grain reserves in Ningbo's affiliated counties has been completed. The Datong News Agency reports that Yu Qiaqing and others have launched the Ningbo-affiliated County Grain Purchasing Association. Fund-raising Association

The increase in rice in the first ten days of the month was 41,061 shi, and the increase in grain was 3,338,800 jin, equivalent to 16,694 shi of rice. The sales of rice in the current ten days of the month were 19,578 shi, and the sales of grain were 1,370,600 jin, equivalent to 6,853 shi of rice. The current storage of rice is 87,934 shi, and the storage of grain is 483 shi (including 5,077 shi of rice from Shanghai, 15,038 shi of rice from Wenzhou and Taizhou, 234 shi of wheat from Wenzhou and Taizhou, and 500 shi of rice from Xiangshan).

Qingxin School Teacher Shen Xuechun Dies, Wife and Concubine Dispute, Wife Alleges Husband's Death Was Caused by Concubine's Harm, Court Autopsy Confirms Death Was Due to Illness 112

Shen Xuechun, a 43-year-old teacher at Qingxin Middle School on Lujiabang Road outside the Great South Gate in Shanghai, earned a monthly salary of 100 yuan. His wife, Gong, 38, lived in Tangmuqiao in the countryside of Chuansha, Pudong. She was a pediatrician, earned a good income, and lived comfortably. However, they had no children after their marriage. Shen had taken a concubine, Xu (named Xinbao), from Xujiahui, Shanghai, who gave birth to one son and two daughters. The son had died young. The eldest daughter, Minfen, was 12, and the younger daughter, Minfang, was 10. Due to disagreements, Shen separated from the concubine and paid her 10 yuan per month. He took back the two daughters and sent them to the countryside to be raised by his wife. Shen then took a Suzhou prostitute, Yin, 35, as his concubine in Shanghai. They had lived together for eleven years, renting a house in the Yuxingfang on Shenfu Road in the French Concession. Shen and Yin were both addicted to opium. His monthly salary was used to pay his wife a monthly allowance of 20 yuan, his former concubine 10 yuan, and a 10 yuan club fee. Only 60 yuan remained for living expenses, leading to financial difficulties. As a result, Shen suffered from liver and stomach disease, which flared up intermittently. On the 19th of this month, Shen's liver and stomach disease relapsed. He took leave from work and stayed at home to seek medical treatment, but it was ineffective. He died on the morning of the 22nd. His concubine, Yin, sent someone to the countryside to inform his wife to come to Shanghai to handle the funeral. Shen's wife, Gong, did not arrive in Shanghai until the morning of the 23rd with relatives, without bringing any expenses. The deceased's concubine, Gu, had already prepared clothing and a coffin. When the wife arrived, the undertaker prepared to dress the deceased for the coffin. However, Shen's wife, Gong, discovered blue and purple spots on the deceased's body, suspecting that they were bruises from being beaten by the concubine. She started a quarrel, accusing the concubine Gu, but the matter could not be resolved. Therefore, Gong insisted that her husband had died from injuries inflicted by the concubine and reported the matter to the French police that afternoon, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the morgue of the Tongren Fuyuan branch hospital for an autopsy. The next day, the Second Special Court was requested to send prosecutor Wang Ren, forensic doctors, and clerks to the hospital to verify that Shen Xuechun had died from illness. Since he had been dead for three days, the blood had stagnated in the corpse, causing the blue and purple spots. There was no other cause. After the officials questioned the deceased's wife and concubine, they ordered that the body be claimed by the deceased's wife, Shen Gong, after she signed a guarantee. After the autopsy, the family followed religious customs to collect the body and transport it back to the countryside for burial. The case of the wife and concubine quarreling over the cause of the husband's death, suspected to be due to injuries, was dismissed after the facts became clear.

Since autumn, this city has experienced little rainfall, causing farmers in the Shanghai suburbs to eagerly await rain. Although there was heavy fog yesterday morning, the weather also turned overcast, creating a sense of rain. Unfortunately, the fog soon dissipated and the sun shone brightly. Fog Yesterday Morning

The weather this autumn has been mostly sunny with little rain, gradually leading to drought conditions. Farmers are eagerly awaiting rain. The dry weather also makes it difficult to regulate one's health. Infectious diseases such as diphtheria are quite rampant. At dawn yesterday, heavy fog suddenly arose, and the sky also turned overcast, creating a strong sense of rain. However, after 8:00 AM, the fog dissipated and the sun shone brightly.

High Tide Expected

Although the sun reappeared after the fog dissipated, the weather was very humid. The ground in shady areas was slightly slippery. Therefore, it is generally speculated that there may be heavy rain within the day. According to the Shanghai Dredging Bureau's predictions, due to the moon's proximity to the earth, there will be a high tide in the Huangpu River on the 30th of this month. The tide will occur at the hour of zi (11:00 PM) on the 30th (estimated to be 11 feet 3 inches) and at the hour of wu (11:00 AM) (estimated to be 11 feet 8 inches), leaving only a little over a foot of clearance from the Bund embankment.

The River Level Continues to Drop, Making Navigation Difficult Between Shanghai and Hankou; The Reason for the Sudden Decrease is Scant Rainfall; Customs Has Set Up Draft Restriction Signs 116

According to Datong News Agency, since the water level of the Yangtze River drastically dropped, navigation for ships in the middle reaches from Hankou to Changsha has become difficult. Shipping companies have already begun to charge extra for shallow water. As for the lower reaches between Shanghai and Hankou, because the river level is still gradually decreasing, navigation will also gradually become more challenging. This is indeed something that deserves great attention. Now, we will explore the details of the situation as follows:

Last Year's Simultaneous Water Level Shows a Significant Disparity

A reporter specially visited Mr. Chen Renzheng, the chief of general affairs at the Ning Shao Shipping Company, to inquire whether the current decline in river levels would cause difficulties for shipping between Shanghai and Hankou in the lower reaches. According to Mr. Chen, the recent drastic drop in the Yangtze River's water level to just over ten feet is a rare occurrence in recent decades. Even at this time last year, the water level was still between thirty-six and thirty-seven feet. Compared with this year, the sudden drop of twenty feet can be described as an anomaly.

Continuous Decline Requires Reducing Draft

Mr. Chen continued, the Ning Jing vessel of the company recently came to Shanghai from Hankou. When passing through the Prince Reef, where the water is shallowest, it was personally measured and the water level was only seventeen feet. However, ships sailing between Shanghai and Hankou, carrying passengers and cargo, have a maximum draft of about twelve or thirteen feet, so there is currently no impact. If the river level continues to decline, dropping to around ten feet, it is possible to reduce the passenger and cargo load to lighten the ship's draft and adapt to the water level.

Reason for the Sudden Decrease: Scant Rainfall

Mr. Chen continued to say, since the current lowest water level is still sixteen or seventeen feet, there are no immediate difficulties for navigation in the lower reaches. However, special caution should be exercised. If a ship runs aground, it can impede the navigation of other vessels. Therefore, pilots must be particularly careful during this shallow water period. Regarding the earlier arrival of the Yangtze River's shallow water season this year, Mr. Chen said it is due to the recent lack of rainfall in the Yangtze River basin, which has caused the river to dry up. He hopes for abundant rainfall soon, which would not only benefit shipping on the Yangtze River, but also provide sufficient water for the fields.

Customs Sets Up Draft Restriction Signs

The Jianghai Customs River Patrol Office, to provide guidance for upstream vessels during the shallow water season, has set up draft restriction signs in Wuhu, indicating the water level readings along the route above Wuhu. This allows all vessels going from Shanghai to Hankou to have something to follow. These draft signs are also equipped with lights, so they are clearly visible even at night. It is also understood that the draft of all river vessels must be lower than the water level by six inches to ensure safety.

Verdict in the Embezzlement Case of the Shanghai Branch Manager of Yumin Bank; Wu Sentenced to Two Years and Qian to Five Years; The Bank Seeks to Recover 800,000 Yuan 117

The embezzlement case involving Qian Yuzhai, the deputy general manager of the Jiangxi Yumin Bank headquarters, and Wu Meisun, the manager of the Shanghai branch, has been judged by the court. The bank has filed a civil lawsuit seeking to recover 800,000 yuan. The details are recorded below:

Suspension from Duty for Investigation

Jiangxi Yumin Bank is a joint public-private venture with a capital of one million yuan, half from the public and half from the private sector. In March of this year, the public shares were increased by one million yuan, bringing the total to two million yuan. Chen Wei was appointed as the general manager and Qian Chengxin as the manager. After auditing the accounts, they discovered that Qian Yuzhai, the deputy general manager of the headquarters, and Wu Meisun, the manager of the Shanghai branch, had committed embezzlement. In July, they reported the matter to the provincial government, which ordered the provincial public security bureau to arrest Qian and Wu and transfer them to the High Court Procuratorate for handling. The Nanchang District Court Procurator was also ordered to investigate. At the same time, Qian and Wu were suspended from their duties. After two months, the investigation was completed, and public prosecution was approved.

Verdict and Sentencing

The case was judged by the Nanchang District Court a few days ago: (1) Wu Meisun, the manager of the Shanghai branch, was found guilty of breach of trust and sentenced to two years of imprisonment. The facts are that on November 26 of last year, the Shanghai branch purchased 580,000 yuan in public bonds for the headquarters to collect coupons. At that time, it was not reported to the headquarters or recorded in the accounts, and the transaction slips were not sent to the headquarters for review. It was only reported to the headquarters after the price dropped, causing losses to the bank. The detailed account prices reported did not match, and the procedures were incomplete, indicating speculative and profiteering behavior by purchasing public bonds through the bank. (2) Qian Yuzhai, the deputy general manager of the headquarters, was found guilty of embezzling items held in the course of business and sentenced to four years of imprisonment. He was also found guilty of continuous breach of trust and sentenced to three years of imprisonment, resulting in a total sentence of five years of imprisonment. The facts are omitted.

Bank Seeks Compensation

Now, Chen Wei, the general manager of the headquarters, has filed a civil lawsuit with the court, seeking compensation from Qian Yuzhai, the former deputy general manager of the headquarters, and Wu Meisun, the manager of the Shanghai branch, for the 800,000 yuan in national currency lost by the bank due to embezzlement. It is said that the court will hear the case.

The Machine-Made Noodle Industry Association Requests a Limit on the Market Price of Flour; Document Submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau 121

The Shanghai Machine-Made Noodle Industry Association, recognizing that flour is an important food for residents, has been greatly affected by the recent soaring market prices. Most of the businesses in the industry are small-scale, and they have suffered huge losses, resulting in daily closures. If no measures are taken to suppress prices, it will be difficult to maintain. Therefore, yesterday, it specifically requested the Social Affairs Bureau to limit the market price in order to remedy the situation. Not only will the industry benefit, but the livelihood of the people and the foundation of the nation will also depend on it. The original document is as follows:

"Presented for the soaring price of flour, which is related to the future of the people's livelihood and affects the safety of the country, we request that your bureau order a limit on the price, prohibit exports, crack down on speculation and manipulation, balance the market situation, and maintain the people's food supply and the stability of the business community. It is believed that flour is a necessity for the people's food supply, and the rise and fall of its price, and the amount of its production and sales, should be subject to unified control and regulations by the country, so as to balance supply and demand and eliminate the evils of speculation and monopoly. If it is allowed to run its natural course, then many evils will arise. Not only will operators be affected, but the people will also encounter the panic of high food prices and the inability to maintain a livelihood, which is related to the safety of the country. According to reports, wheat has had a bumper harvest in various places this year, which is sufficient to meet the needs of the country and should not lead to price increases. Unexpectedly, during this tense time of national crisis, flour prices have soared, rising rapidly without end. This is obviously caused by unscrupulous merchants manipulating and speculating in secret. If it is not stopped, not only will the impact on our industry be worrisome, but also the future of the people's food supply will be greatly affected. The association does not dare to remain silent and especially appeals to your bureau to quickly stipulate the maximum price of flour, not exceeding three yuan and three cents per bag, and prohibit exports, hoping that you will review and approve the order for implementation, so that the society and the business community will benefit from it. This is the presentation."

The Old Site of the Central Police Station is Developed into a Parking Lot; Monthly Fee is Five Yuan, Daily Fee is Fifty Cents 125

After the Central Police Station of the Municipal Council was rebuilt with a new building, a portion of the site has been leased to a Westerner, Molian, for use as a daily automobile parking lot. The parking fee is five yuan per car per month, and fifty cents per day. For less than one day, it is thirty cents. The lease term is stipulated to end on December 30. To recover the lease after that, six months' notice is required. The lot can park ninety-six cars.

Bandits Block a Westerner's Car 126

A Westerner, Kelinglin, was driving his private black-plated car No. 8067 from east to west along Jing'an Temple Road at 1:00 AM this morning. When he was about to pass the intersection of Hardoon Road, three bandits suddenly jumped out, each holding a pistol, blocking his way. Kelinglin, seeing that the situation was not good, quickly stepped on the accelerator and rushed forward. The bandits were unable to stop him and had to retreat. One of the bandits pulled out a gun and fired at the car before fleeing. The bullet penetrated the rear car window glass and the car shell, but fortunately did not hit him. Afterwards, Kelinglin drove to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station to report the incident and requested an investigation. Detectives found a shell casing at the scene of the incident and brought it back to the police station for safekeeping.

The Ministry of Interior Issues a Copyright Certificate for the Standard Chinese Typeface Copper Mold 132

The Standard Chinese Movable Typeface, created by the famous painters Zheng Wuchang, Chen Xiaodie, Li Zuhan, Zhu Xinpei, etc., has elegant and neat characters and has long been popular at home and abroad. There are distribution and agency offices in Japan, North America, Southeast Asia, and other places. It is a great contribution to modern China's cultural undertakings. The movable typeface was submitted to the Ministry of Industry for reservation of patent rights. Recently, in order to expand business and protect rights and interests, Mr. Zheng and others applied to the Ministry of Interior for registration and have received the approval of the Ministry of Interior to issue Copyright Certificate No. Jingzi 7734.

There is Donghualu of the eleven Qing Dynasty, one hundred and twenty-four volumes, printed in letterpress, sold for twelve yuan. There is "Hu Linyi's Reading History and Military Strategy", twelve volumes for eight jiao. "Ming Tong Jian", sixteen volumes for one yuan and four jiao. There is a pocket-sized edition of "Kojiki", six volumes for five jiao. The complete works of Guan Gong, compiled by Qian Muzhai, exquisitely bound in a thick volume, is sold for three jiao. There are many books, and a catalog is available.

Weather Report 140

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather would be clear with a strong northwest wind, due to a low pressure passing through the Yellow Sea and moving northeast-east. The Yellow River basin would be cloudy to clear, with sand and a northwest wind. The wind force in the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River would be unstable. There would be southwest to northwest winds in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The East China Sea and Taiwan would be cloudy with strong northeast winds. The Pacific hurricane would continue to move west or northwest-west. Its center had advanced to within about one hundred and ten miles of 18 degrees north latitude and 132 degrees east longitude at 2:00 PM in the afternoon. The wind force was not known. Also, within the twenty-four hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the port was 84.7 degrees and the lowest was 60.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 76.3 degrees and the lowest was 66.2 degrees.

Shanghai Municipal Brokerage Goods Tariff Table:

Fourth Class: Vegetable Brokers, Bamboo Shoot Brokers, Radish Brokers, Sweet Potato Brokers, Mulberry Seedling Brokers, Grass Seed Brokers, Reed Mat Brokers, Rush Shoe Brokers, Bran Brokers, Alum and Alkali Brokers, Flower Brokers, Snail Brokers, Honeybee Brokers, Rope Brokers, Firewood and Grass Brokers, Boat Repair Brokers, Circle Ash Brokers, Thatching Straw Brokers, Straw Paper Brokers, Bean Dregs Brokers, Pig and Cow Blood Brokers, Yellow Sand and Gravel Brokers, Sun-Dried Bran and Wood Chip Brokers.

Revised Detailed Rules for the Collection of Brokerage Tax by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance:

Article 1: These detailed rules are formulated in accordance with Article 28 of the Shanghai Municipal Brokerage Business Regulations.

Article 2: All existing brokerage firms within the Shanghai city area that have already received registration certificates from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, regardless of whether they are long-term or short-term, shall have their certificates inspected by the Inspection and Collection Department of this Bureau. Certificates that have not expired shall be stamped with a "Verified" mark and remain valid. Certificates that have expired shall be immediately ordered to be renewed.

Article 3: All applications for registration certificates shall be investigated and processed by personnel dispatched by this Bureau.

Article 4: All brokerage firms that have been approved for licensing shall have their long-term and short-term goods tax rates registered separately by this Bureau, and the relevant Inspection and Collection Department shall be ordered to issue certificates and collect taxes in accordance with the regulations.

Article 5: When each Inspection and Collection Department collects brokerage tax, in addition to issuing receipts for the annual business tax, overdue tax payments, and late fees for long-term brokerage firms, the registration tax for long-term brokerage firms and the registration and business taxes for short-term brokerage firms shall all be based on the registration certificate, and no separate receipts shall be issued.

Article 6: Brokerage registration certificates and business tax receipts for long-term brokerage firms shall be printed by this Bureau and issued to each Inspection and Collection Department for use, all in quadruplicate. The first copy shall be given to the brokerage firm, the second copy shall be submitted for verification, the third copy shall be reported for inspection, and the fourth copy shall be kept as a record.

Article 7: Receipts for fines shall be issued using the Bureau's ordinary four-part receipt.

Article 8: Each Inspection and Collection Department shall designate an employee to be responsible for investigating brokerage matters.

Article 9: If personnel inspecting brokerage firms find that certificates have not been renewed upon expiration or that taxes have been underpaid, they shall strictly urge the firms to renew their certificates and pay taxes. If unlicensed operation, impersonation, substitution, multiple use of a single license, or alteration of certificates is discovered, the relevant Inspection and Collection Department shall be immediately notified for verification. If necessary, the local police station of the Public Security Bureau may be notified to assist in the handling of the matter.

Article 10: Any matters not covered by these detailed rules shall be amended as needed and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record.

Article 11: These detailed rules shall be submitted to the Ministry of Finance and presented to the Executive Yuan for approval and record, and shall be promulgated and implemented by the Municipal Government.

Sports News

The City's Fourth Annual Municipal Games Closed Yesterday - Dat-sha, Chih-tse, Physical Education School, Teachers' College, and Tung-a Won Championships - Awards Ceremony to be Held on Another Date 142

The fourth annual municipal games, sponsored by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, concluded successfully yesterday morning after two and a half days of competition. The men's championship in the college group went to Da Xia, while the men's championships in the physical education school and teachers' college groups both went to Tung-a. The awards ceremony will be held on another date. Overall, although the games were somewhat disorganized on the first day due to the excessive number of groups and the complexity of the affairs, the situation improved after the second day. The officials and athletes were in good spirits. Although the results were not entirely satisfactory, there were few unnecessary disputes during the games.

Due to changes in the regulations, this year's games were not held according to the old rules, so it is impossible to compare the records with previous years. However, a table comparing the best results of each group with the highest records of the municipal games shows that in women's track and field, seven records were broken and one was tied, excluding the 50-meter dash and the long jump. In men's track and field, only the discus record was broken, with the others falling far short. Two conclusions can be drawn from this: (1) The women's results were better than the men's, and the results of the female physical education teachers were even better. It is also unusual that the men's high jump results in the college and physical education school groups were not as good as those in the high school group. (2) The highest records of the municipal games were set three years ago, as the third municipal games organized by the Municipal Bureau of Education were held in 1933. This indicates that the athletic performance of men in this city has not improved in the past three years, and those responsible for sports should pay close attention to this.

Preliminary Round Yesterday - Hong Kong Lai Wah Cup - Hua Lian Defeats Army - Clerks Defeat Navy 143

(Hong Kong, 25th) In the preliminary round of the Lai Wah Cup football tournament, held on the 25th, Hua Lian faced the Army team. Veteran players Li Huitang, the Four Knights (Bao Jiaping, Mai Shaohan, Huang Meishun), Liang Rongzhao, Chen Hongguang, and others were unable to participate. The team was composed of new players such as Huang Hua, Ji Liangxian, Zan Linde, Pu Hezuoxian, Zeng Zhongyun, and Yang Benhan. Many spectators believed that the team was not strong enough and would surely lose. However, the result was unexpected. After 20 minutes of overtime, Dehui scored another goal, giving the team a 4-3 victory. At the same time, the Clerks' team defeated the Navy team 4-1. Hua Lian and the Clerks will compete for the championship next time.

Western League Group C Match - Yousheng Ties Tongwen - Result 2-2 145

The Development Process of the Japanese Silk Industry 147

— Deng Baoguang

(I) The Value of the Silk Industry in the Japanese Economy

Sericulture is the second largest agricultural product in Japan after rice. The silk reeling industry is Japan's oldest and a fundamental modern industry. Silk fabrics are Japan's largest export in international trade. Therefore, the silk industry occupies a crucial position in Japan's rural economy, capitalist economic structure, and international trade balance.

The Japanese silk industry not only holds an important position in Japan but also dominates the world. Japan is the world's largest producer of raw silk and the largest exporter of silk fabrics.

(I) Value in Farm Household Economy

The importance of sericulture in Japan's agricultural economy is clearly demonstrated by the ratio of sericulture households and the ratio of production prices.

In the first year of the Taisho era, Japan had 5.438 million farm households, of which 1.5 million were sericulture households, accounting for approximately 27.6% of the total. This number gradually increased, and by the fourth year of the Showa era, the number of sericulture households reached 2.217 million out of a total of 5.576 million farm households, accounting for 39.8% of the total. Subsequently, due to the global economic panic, silk prices plummeted, and Japanese rural areas were the first to suffer a significant blow. Consequently, the number of sericulture farmers gradually decreased. By the ninth year of the Showa era, sericulture farmers accounted for 1.995 million out of 5.617 million households, representing 35.5% of the total.

Rice is Japan's largest agricultural product, and cocoons are the second largest. According to statistics from the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry in the third year of the Showa era, the total value of agricultural production was over 3.8 billion yuan, with rice accounting for over 1.8 billion yuan and cocoons accounting for over 660 million yuan, approximately 1.7% of the total. In the fourth year of the Showa era, the total value of agricultural products was 3.48 billion yuan, and cocoons were worth over 550 million yuan, accounting for slightly less than 16%. The seventh year of the Showa era was the most economically depressed year for Japanese rural areas. The total value of agricultural products decreased to about 2 billion yuan, and the value of cocoons decreased to 297 million yuan, accounting for 12%.

Although cocoons are the second largest agricultural product in Japan after rice, they occupy a position above rice in terms of Japanese farm household income. This is because Japanese agriculture is still dominated by small farmers, and the rice produced by small farmers is mostly consumed by themselves. Therefore, there is hardly any rice available for sale. However, the cocoons produced by ordinary farm households are all commercial goods, making cocoons the largest source of cash income for sericulture farmers. Therefore, the economic value of sericulture in Japanese agriculture is even more important.

(II) Value in Industrial Economy

In the seventh year of the Showa era, the total value of Japan's industrial production was over 5.98 billion yuan, and the value of raw silk and silk fabrics reached 590 million yuan, accounting for 9.7% of the total. In the ninth year of the Showa era, due to the prosperity of military demand and export industries, the value of industrial production increased to 9.39 billion yuan. However, raw silk and silk fabrics decreased to over 560 million yuan due to the impact of the global economic panic, and the ratio to total production value relatively decreased to 5.9%. Nevertheless, it remains an important sector in Japan's industrial economy.

Furthermore, according to statistics from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in the ninth year of the Showa era, there were 80,300 factories in Japan employing five or more workers, with silk reeling factories accounting for over 5,000. Of the 2.13 million workers in Japan, over 360,000 were employed in the silk reeling industry. This also fully demonstrates its considerable importance.

(III) Value in International Trade

Silk fabrics are Japan's largest surplus commodity in international trade and occupy a special position in the international balance of payments. This is a rare phenomenon in the impoverished Japanese economic structure, from raw material manufacturing to export.

In the third year of the Showa era, Japan's total international trade exports amounted to 1.9722 billion yuan, with silk fabrics accounting for 878 million yuan, representing 44% of total exports. In the sixth year of the Showa era, Japan's export trade decreased to 1.41 billion yuan, and silk fabric exports also decreased to 400 million yuan due to the global recession, reducing the proportion of total exports to 28%. In the tenth year of the Showa era, Japan's export trade surged to 2.48 billion yuan, with silk fabrics accounting for 479 million yuan, relatively decreasing the proportion of total exports to 15%. Although the export value of silk fabrics has gradually decreased due to the global economic recession, the general decline in purchasing power, and the atmosphere of expanding military demand and the activity of some export industries in Japan, it remains the largest source of revenue in Japan's international balance of payments.

(II) Current Status of the Japanese Silk Industry

The Japanese silk industry is also following the path of Japanese capitalist economic development and progressing upward step by step. In the early Meiji era, during the process of Japan's economic construction, efforts were made to increase silk production, improve technology, and expand international trade without any reservation. In the Meiji 22-26 era, the silk production volume was only 1.1 million kan (Note 1), and the export trade volume at that time was only 19 million yuan. By the Meiji 44 era, the production volume increased to over 3.4 million kan, and the export volume increased to over 129 million yuan. In 20 years, the degree of development tripled, and exports increased sevenfold. Subsequently, the outbreak of the European War further developed the Japanese silk industry. Before the war, in the third year of the Taisho era, the production volume was 3.75 million kan, and the export volume was 160 million yuan. After the end of the European War, in the eighth year of the Taisho era, the production volume reached 6.36 million kan, and the export volume reached over 623 million yuan.

The reasons for the leap forward in the Japanese silk industry are twofold: (1) government encouragement and promotion, and (2) the stimulus of the general economic development of Japan and the expansion of the international market. Regarding the former, the government encouraged farmers to raise silkworms and promoted exports. The Export Promotion Law was promulgated on April 1, Meiji 21. In the 33rd year, the export tax of 123 yuan and 61 sen per 100 yuan was abolished, and funds were loaned to purchase new machinery to improve technology. In the Meiji 22-26 era, those using machinery accounted for 41%, and those using old-fashioned production methods accounted for 59%. By the Meiji 44 era, those using machinery accounted for 70%, and those using old-fashioned methods accounted for only 30%. In terms of sericulture, production methods also progressed, and even in terms of quality, there was a significant upward trend. In the early Meiji era, the cocoon harvest per cho (Note 2) of mulberry garden was only 7 kan. By the 40th year of Meiji, the average increase in harvest reached 9 kan, and the maximum reached 11 kan. By the eighth year of the Showa era, it increased to over 15 kan. Because of the progress in production technology, the ratio of mulberry gardens to cultivated land and the ratio of sericulture farmers have only increased by 25% from the early Meiji era to the present, but the production volume has increased sixfold, and the export volume has increased six hundredfold. Regarding the latter, during the period when various economic sectors in Japan were developing upward, such as the textile industry, transportation, various basic industries, and the cultural level of the people, coupled with the stimulus of the markets and colonies seized after the Sino-Japanese War, the Russo-Japanese War, and the European War, Japan leaped to the throne of the world silk industry.

Since the global economic panic of 1929, the Japanese silk industry has been hit hard. Originally, sericulture in Japan had been the only clothing material since ancient times due to the lack of cotton. Therefore, during the shogunate era before the Meiji Restoration, the export of silk was strictly prohibited several times. By the time of the Meiji Restoration, the emerging textile industry gradually rose, and the large amount of cotton yarn imported into Japan from the United Kingdom, as well as the cotton yarn and cotton fabrics produced domestically, gradually replaced the position of silk fabrics. Therefore, present-day Japan has changed from a silk fabric-based country to a cotton fabric-based country, and silk fabrics have become an export commodity. As a result, Japan's silk fabric exports have been increasing year by year as previously mentioned. The relationship with the international economy and the dependence on international trade have also gradually expanded. Therefore, changes in the world economy are fully reflected in the Japanese silk industry. Hence, when the global economic panic struck, the Japanese silk industry was the first to be hit.

Due to the prosperity after the European War, the export value of Japanese raw silk and silk fabrics reached 878 million yuan in the third year of the Showa era and 943 million yuan in the fourth year of the Showa era. In the fifth year of the Showa era, affected by the global economic panic, the export value drastically decreased to 488 million yuan, of which raw silk accounted for 419 million yuan and silk fabrics accounted for 68 million yuan. The export destinations of silk fabrics were mainly India and Australia, followed by the United Kingdom and Manchuria. Because Japanese silk fabrics are high-end products, buyers are mostly wealthy people. Therefore, even in the autumn of the global economic panic, silk fabrics were still able to maintain their original position. However, raw silk was different. The largest export product among Japanese silk products is raw silk, and the most important export destination for raw silk is the United States. In the 14th year of the Taisho era, Japan's raw silk export value was 877 million yuan, and the amount imported into the United States reached 844 million yuan, accounting for 96.4% of the total. In the fifth year of the Showa era, due to the general global recession, Japan's raw silk export value drastically decreased to 419 million yuan, and the proportion exported to the United States decreased to 95%. In the ninth year of the Showa era, due to the severity of the global recession and the prevention policies of various countries against Japanese goods, Japan's raw silk export value decreased to 287 million yuan, creating the lowest record in more than ten years. Although it recovered to 387 million yuan in the tenth year of the Showa era, it is still a major threat in the lame economic process of Japan. Moreover, there are two noteworthy phenomena in the process of shrinking exports: (1) The export value decreased by 51%, while the export volume only decreased by 5%. The fact that this expresses is that silk prices plummeted. Although the plummeting of silk prices is a major threat to the Japanese industrial economy, it is a fatal blow to the Japanese rural economy. This point is clearly demonstrated by the bankruptcy of the Japanese rural economy in recent years. (2) The amount imported into the United States accounted for 96.5% of the total in the fourth year of the Showa era, gradually decreasing to 84.1% last year. This trend is expected to continue to decline. On the contrary, exports to Europe have increased from 2.3% to 11.8%. This proves that the dependence of the Japanese silk industry on the United States is gradually decreasing, while the dependence on European countries is gradually deepening. Now, the table of the recent Japanese raw silk export value and regional relationship ratio is as follows:

Japanese Raw Silk Export Status Table

(Note) Export amount unit: 1 million pounds, export value unit: 1 million yuan, the ratio is 100 in Showa 4, and the export destination amount is 100.

(1) The status of Japanese silk production during the panic process. As previously stated, the dependence of the Japanese silk industry and international trade is profound. Therefore, the changes in the prosperity and decline of the international economy proportionately dominate the entire Japanese silk industry. The climax of the global economic panic invaded various departments in 1929, and the Japanese silk industry, which was directly dominated, also underwent tremendous changes.

The production value of Japanese cocoons was 84.8 million kan in the 14th year of the Taisho era, with a total value of over 814 million yuan. In the 4th year of the Showa era, the total production value decreased to 10.2 million kan, but the total value decreased to 655 million yuan. In the 5th year of the Showa era, the global economic panic struck. Although the production value continued to increase to 10.6 million kan, the total value drastically decreased to 304 million yuan. Afterwards, it decreased year by year. In the 8th year of the Showa era, it once recovered to 500 million yuan. However, in the 9th year of the Showa era, the production value decreased to 87 million kan due to the successive attacks of severe wind and flood disasters, cold disasters, and droughts, and the total value fell to 202.8 million yuan. Compared with the highest record in the 14th year of the Taisho era, it decreased by 75%, which is indeed the biggest blow to the Japanese rural economy since the Meiji Restoration. Therefore, since the 4th year of Showa, the number of sericulture households has decreased from 2.3 million to 1.99 million, and the area of mulberry gardens has decreased from 714,000 cho to 623,000 cho. After that, there is still a tendency to decrease.

The raw silk production status also changes with the stages of the global economic prosperity and decline. In the 14th year of the Taisho era, the total raw silk production value was 8.28 million kan, with a total value of 956 million yuan. In the 3rd year of the Showa era, the production value increased to 10.58 million kan, and the total value decreased to 835 million yuan. In the 5th year of the Showa era, the production value increased to 11.36 million kan, and the value decreased to 536 million yuan. By the 9th year of the Showa era, the production value increased again to 12 million kan, the highest record in Japanese production, but the value decreased to 398 million yuan, the lowest record in nearly 20 years. The value increased to 488 million yuan in the 10th year of the Showa era, so the situation last year and this year has some hope of recovery compared with the 9th year of the Showa era.

Although cocoon prices and raw silk prices have plummeted, and the total production value has fallen by 25%-29%, the production value of silk fabrics still maintains its original state. This means that silk fabrics are consumables for special classes. Although the world is in such a recession, the consumables of special classes can still maintain their original state. This proves the class nature of the panic. The production price of Japanese silk fabrics was 327 million yuan in the 5th year of the Showa era. In the 9th year of the Showa era, the most economically depressed year for the Japanese silk industry, the total production value of silk fabrics increased to 341 million yuan, and it continued to increase to 349 million yuan in the 10th year of the Showa era. After that, there is still hope for increase.

Japanese cocoon, raw silk, and silk fabric production status

(Note) Production amount unit: 1,000 kan, value amount unit: 1,000 yuan.

(2) The impact of the silk industry on the Japanese economy during the panic.

As mentioned earlier, the global economic panic affected the poor performance of Japanese raw silk exports. The poor performance of exports affected the plummeting of silk prices. The plummeting of silk prices directly affected the plummeting of cocoon prices and further affected the interests of silk reeling operators and the income and expenditure of farm households. The scope of the impact of this shadow in the dissemination process is getting bigger and bigger. Therefore, if it is said that the silk industry is the initial driving force of the economic panic in Japan in recent years, it is no exaggeration.

Cocoons are the second largest agricultural product in Japanese rural areas, and they are the only commodity and the only income and expenditure among agricultural products. Therefore, the rise and fall of cocoon prices are the indicators of the economic prosperity and panic of rural areas. The average price of 1 kan of spring cocoons and autumn cocoons in Japan has long been maintained at a level price of 4 to 5 yuan in the Meiji era. After the outbreak of the European War, it gradually rose, and it rose to 11 yuan and 57 sen in the 8th year of the Taisho era, the highest record in modern Japanese history. It was 10 yuan and 58 sen in the 14th year of the Taisho era, and then it gradually declined. It dropped to 7 yuan and 6 sen in the 4th year of Showa, and it drastically dropped to 3 yuan and 10 sen when the world panic struck in the 5th year. It fell to the lowest price of 2 yuan and 45 sen in the 9th year.

The plummeting of cocoon prices severed the only economic source of farm households, and the rural economy had to fall into bankruptcy. Typical evidence of rural bankruptcy in Japan, such as the total amount of debt in Japanese rural areas, was only 1.3 billion yuan in the era of Taisho 14. However, according to the latest survey estimates, it will reach 6 billion yuan. Therefore, in the current Japanese rural areas, banks and landlords are rising, and more and more poor farmers are selling green seedlings and cold silkworms (Note 3) at low prices when they are in short supply. The hungry children in rural areas are even more concentrated in the cities, which affects the living conditions of the general working class in the cities. Therefore, labor wages are falling and labor hours are extending, creating the bankruptcy of the entire Japanese working class in recent years.

The same bankrupt phenomena are occurring in the silk reeling industry as in the rural areas. In the 14th year of Taisho, there were 3,643 factories in Japan using mechanical silk reeling, and the number of spindles was 276,000. It was reduced to 235,000, 3,260 factories in Showa 10, and the number of spindles was also reduced from 162,000 to 48,000. This gradual decline is, of course, the result of elimination during the panic.

(3) The scale of silk reeling and various equipment.

Although Japan is the kingdom of silk in the current century, its business form still maintains the operating methods of handicraft industry and even family industry. Therefore, small and medium-sized factories account for an absolute majority of more than 90% and hold a dominant position in the Japanese silk industry.

According to statistics from the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, in the 14th year of Taisho, there were 110,000 weaving machine factories. More than 104,800 factories had less than 5 machines, accounting for 94% of the total. There were more than 2,900 factories with 5 to 10 machines, more than 2,400 factories with 10 to 50 machines, and only 218 factories with more than 50 machines. By the 9th year of Showa, the number of factories with less than 5 machines decreased to 61,800, the number of factories with 5 to 10 machines increased to more than 4,600, the number of factories with 10 to 50 machines increased to more than 5,700, and the number of factories with more than 50 machines increased to 691. The total number of factories decreased to more than 72,900.

Number of Japanese weaving factories

The above table fully proves that Japan's silk reeling industry is still a small-scale family industry. Now, under the elimination of the panic, it has entered a new trend. Small factories are gradually decreasing, and large factories are gradually increasing. However, the transformation of the times to enter a sound path like the textile industry still requires time.

At present, the more healthy business forms are roughly four.

(A) Katakura Silk Reeling: Founded in March of the 9th year of Taisho, with an authorized capital of 53.55 million yuan and a paid-in capital of 26.775 million yuan. It has built 45 factories in the main sericultural areas, with an equipment capacity of 14,950 spindles. The production capacity reached 952,111 kan in the 9th year of Showa, making it the largest silk reeling factory in Japan.

(B) Gunze Silk Reeling: Founded in the 29th year of Meiji, with an authorized capital of 20.6666 million yuan and a paid-in capital of 15.297 million yuan. It has established 23 factories in the main areas across the country, with an equipment capacity of 11,048 spindles. The production amount reached more than 916,000 kan in the 9th year of Showa, making it the most historical silk reeling kingdom in Japan.

(C) Nippon Silk Weaving: Founded in June of the 7th year of Taisho, with an authorized capital of 450,000 yuan and a paid-in capital of 350,000 yuan. It has established 6 factories in various main areas, with more than 34,000 silk weaving spindles and 1,343 weaving machines. The production amount in the first half of the 9th year of Showa was 11,000 tan.

(C) Nippon Spinning: Founded in August of the 7th year of Taisho, with an authorized capital of 1 million yuan and a paid-in capital of 913,000 yuan. It has established a new-style factory in Kiryu City, with 53,000 spinning spindles and a production amount of 32,500 kan.

(4) The future of the Japanese silk industry and the current status of control.

The Japanese silk industry is dominated by the prosperity and decline of the world economy and the changes in international relations. At the current stage, it is impossible to restore the prosperity of the 14th year of Taisho.

At present, the entire international relationship is spinning in the vortex of economic competition among various imperialisms. The entire trade policy is completely dominated by the consciousness of self-sufficiency, forming an economic bloc within its own sphere of influence. Therefore, since the Ottawa Agreement formed the British Bloc, Japanese cotton cloth exports to the British territories have been severely hit. Since the realization of the American Bloc, Japanese exports to the United States have been greatly affected. For example, before 1929, Japanese raw silk exports to the United States accounted for 96% of the total. In recent years, due to the domestic economic recession, weak national purchasing power, and even the increase in tariffs to prevent the import of Japanese goods, the amount of Japanese raw silk exported to the United States has decreased from 54 million pounds to 42 million pounds year by year, and the ratio has decreased from 96.5% to 84.1%. It is difficult for Japanese raw silk dominated by the current American trade policy to restore its original state. In addition, although there has been an increasing tendency in European countries in recent years, there is no room for development under the current changes in international relations and the pressure of trade policies. In addition, the only optimistic one is Manchuria, but due to climate relations and rural economic bankruptcy, there is no possibility of development at present. As for the domestic consumption problem in Japan, it is even more impossible to expect an increase in the purchase of silk fabrics in today's rural economic depression, small and medium-sized business and industry recession, and low living standards of the working class.

The Japanese silk industry cannot be optimistic in the international market, and cannot be expected in the internal market. A strong regulatory agency appeared in this panic process of being in a dilemma. The regulatory agency is also a means of trade policy in the economic panic process, a way to break through the status quo, control production internally, and encourage progress in living technology, and develop the market externally.

Originally, the regulatory facilities of the Japanese silk industry had the establishment of the silk industry cooperative in the 44th year of Meiji. In the 15th year of Taisho, it was changed to the Central Association of Silk Industry Cooperative. It comprehensively guides and controls the affairs of the silk industry. Until the 59th Congress of the 6th year of Showa, the Silk Industry Cooperation Law was promulgated. Based on this law, the Japan Central Silk Association was established. In March of the 7th year of Showa, the Central Association of Silk Industry Cooperative was dissolved, and it became the highest regulatory agency of the current Japanese silk industry.

Under the guidance of the government's trade policy, the Japan Central Silk Association controls the Japanese silk affairs. Its organizational outline is roughly as follows:

Japan Central Silk Association

National Sericulture Industry Cooperative Federation - Prefectural Sericulture Federation - County/City Sericulture Industry Federation

National Silkworm Seed Industry Cooperative Federation - Prefectural Silkworm Seed Industry Federation - Silkworm Seed Industry Manufacturers

National Industry and Silk Reeling Industry Cooperative Federation - Prefectural Industry and Silk Reeling Cooperation - Silk Reeling Industry Industry Cooperative

National Silk Reeling Industry Cooperative Federation - Prefectural Silk Reeling Industry Cooperation - Silk Reeling Operators

National Raw Silk Sales Cooperative Federation - County/City Raw Silk Sales Industry Cooperation - Raw Silk Sales Federation

National Raw Silk Export Industry Cooperative Federation - City Raw Silk Export Industry Cooperation - Raw Silk Export Federation

〇 Special Council

(Note) □ Group 〇 Individual

(3) The Development of the Japanese Silk Industry and the Chinese Silk Industry

Silk has a longer history in China than in Japan. For thousands of years, it has been used as the only clothing material. Until cotton was introduced from India during the Yuan Dynasty, it gradually seized the inherent position of silk, and silk products became luxury items. Since the end of the Qing Dynasty, the mechanical industry has flourished, and international trade relations have become increasingly close. Therefore, the silk industry has become the only export product of China for a time. It not only occupies a special position in China's foreign trade but also holds the most important position in China's rural economy and even industrial economy. Since the development of Japanese silk, due to the government's policy of encouraging exports and the progress of production technology, China's inherent silk market in Europe and the United States has been gradually encroached upon, and the Chinese silk industry has gradually fallen into the abyss. China's raw silk export trade reached more than 148 million yuan in the 11th year of the Republic of China, accounting for 22% of the total trade exports. In the 18th year of the Republic of China, the export value reached 165 million yuan. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, it dropped to 95 million yuan, and it further dropped to 36 million yuan in the 21st year, reaching an unprecedented low record. This is in the Chinese rural economy, especially the rural areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, on the verge of bankruptcy. In the Chinese industrial economy, 107 silk reeling factories in Shanghai and Wuxi, more than 90 factories stopped work. In China's international trade, it lost a major compensation amount, and the impact will not only be the bankruptcy of one part of the silk industry.

In short, the decline of the Chinese silk industry is closely related to the rise of the Japanese silk industry, especially the protectionist trade policy implemented by Japan. However, the progress of production technology, the improvement of management methods, and the uniformity of control steps in the Japanese silk industry are also worthy of deep consideration by the people who are being driven out.

October 18, 1936. In Tokyo

(Note 1) One kan is equal to one hundred taels

(Note 2) One cho is approximately equal to 14 mu in China

(Note 3) Green seedlings refer to the sale of grain at a low price when the grain is not yet ripe. Cold silkworms refer to the sale of next spring's cocoons at a low price this winter. This is a high-interest loan with grain and cocoons as collateral.

Artist Jin Xuecheng - Receives Honor in Japan - Selected for the Japan National Art Exhibition - First Honorary Crown for Chinese Students in Japan 151

Young artist Jin Xuecheng, a native of Fengxian County, Jiangsu Province, has been studying sculpture in Japan for eight years. Last year, he graduated from the Tokyo National University of Fine Arts and was at the top of his class. Soon after, he was selected for the Second Division Art Exhibition. At that time, Japanese newspapers praised him extensively and he achieved great honor. His reputation reached China, and many domestic art schools, admiring Jin's name, sent letters of invitation. However, Jin remained true to his artistic sincerity and humbly declined all offers, continuing to immerse himself in artistic research. He diligently pursued his art, and his skills advanced greatly. Recently, the Japan National Art Exhibition, the Bunten, announced that Jin had once again been named to the list. For eight years, Jin's efforts in art have been unwavering, allowing him to rise steadily and achieve great depth. On the day of the announcement, Tokyo newspapers all published Jin's photo with great fanfare, praising him as the first honorary crown for a citizen of the Republic of China. It is said that the authorities at the Tokyo National University of Fine Arts believe that in the over two [missing number] years of the Bunten's history, Jin is the first foreigner to be selected for the Japan National Art Exhibition, so they have submitted a request to the Japanese government to commend him in order to show goodwill and provide encouragement.

Ministry of Education Subsidizes Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Students - Measures for Advancement to Higher Education 153

On the 24th, the Ministry of Education issued a circular to all schools above the junior college level, distributing the 11-article Outline of Measures for Subsidizing Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Students Advancing to Junior Colleges and Universities in the Interior, ordering them to comply with the measures. The original text is as follows: 1. In order to encourage Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students to advance to junior colleges and universities in the interior for further studies, the Ministry of Education will allocate a certain amount from the border education subsidy funds for this purpose starting in the 25th year. 2. The number of subsidized students is set at 15. Those who are admitted to public or registered private junior colleges and universities may apply for subsidies. Students already studying at public or registered private junior colleges and universities may also apply for subsidies according to the same regulations. 3. Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students applying for subsidies must be currently residing in Mongolian, Tibetan areas and Xinjiang Province. 4. Applicants for subsidies must prepare the following documents: (1) Proof of residence from the local administrative agency; (2) Proof of admission from the school they are admitted to; (3) Graduation certificate or certificate from the original graduating middle school; (4) Three recent 4-inch half-length photos. All of the above documents, together with the application form, should be submitted to the Ministry of Education for verification. 5. Students approved for subsidies will receive 300 yuan per year, which will be allocated by the Ministry of Education to the school the student is attending on a monthly basis for distribution to the student. 6. Subsidized students must abide by school regulations and work hard in their studies. If they violate school regulations and are disciplined by the school, or if they neglect their studies and fail more than three subjects, the Ministry of Education may, depending on the severity of the situation, reduce, suspend, or recover the subsidy. 7. All public or registered private junior colleges and universities that have Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students receiving subsidies under this outline of measures should submit the student's conduct and academic performance to the Ministry of Education at the end of each academic year for evaluation. 8. Anyone who falsely claims to be a Mongolian, Tibetan, or Hui student, or impersonates someone else, or forges documents will, if discovered, be subject to recovery of the subsidy in addition to appropriate punishment. 9. Those who receive subsidies from administrative agencies at all levels or receive public funding from schools are not eligible to apply for subsidies. 10. This outline of measures may be revised by the Ministry of Education when necessary. 11. This outline of measures will take effect from the date of promulgation.

Economic Special

Sudden Obstacles to Silk Exports to France 157

— Qian Tianda

(1) Introduction

Chinese silk has suffered from the impact of the global economic panic, the squeeze from Japanese silk, and the dumping of rayon. In recent years, foreign trade has plummeted, almost following in the footsteps of Chinese tea, with a sense of being at the end of its road.

In 1934 (Republic of China Year 23), the national export volume was only 32,977 quintals (approximately 52,773 piculs), worth 23,519,150 yuan (approximately 16,833,788 taels), the lowest export year since the Republic of China and a year of extreme decline. Compared to the peak export year of 1929 with 189,980 bales worth 147,681,388 taels, the quantity was less than one-third and the price was less than one-eighth, truly an extreme decline.

"When things get bad enough, they must get better." After a period of extreme decline, there must be a day of renewed prosperity. This is the principle of the economic cycle. Last year (1935), the global economy gradually recovered after a long period of withering, and the sales of Chinese silk turned around slightly. Furthermore, due to the government's implementation of the new currency policy, foreign trade suddenly became active. Last year, Shanghai alone exported 55,007 bales of raw silk, and Guangdong shipped out 42,231 bales, totaling 97,238 bales. Silk mills in Shanghai and Wuxi also started operations one after another, believing that the golden age was coming again.

This year, due to weather conditions, the silkworm cocoons were of poor quality, and the reeling loss was quite high. Therefore, although the silk market was often at 600-700 yuan, silk mills only barely covered their costs and had no profit. The autumn cocoons also suffered a poor harvest (50% in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces this year), resulting in a shortage of raw materials and high prices for cocoons. Increased costs, if silk prices do not rise and sales are hindered, silk mills will inevitably feel the difficulty of turnover again, and the plight of the previous year may well be repeated today.

Recently, the French government abandoned the gold standard and devalued the franc. The exchange rate between Chinese currency and the French franc suddenly dropped from 464 francs per 100 yuan (September 25) to 630 francs (currently quoted by the Central Bank). Chinese silk transactions suddenly came to a standstill, which has had a significant impact on the export of raw silk from our country. Some believe that our country's exports to France are not important, and that France's silk consumption is small, not as large as that of the United States, so there is no need to worry. In fact, Chinese silk sales to France have their own unique position, which I will explain below.

(2) The Importance of Chinese Silk Sales to France

France has always been a country with a large consumption of silk, and Chinese silk sales to France have a long history. Narrow stripes of 9-11 and 13-15 are specialties of our country, far superior to Japanese silk. Since the outbreak of the European War, the global economic situation has changed, and the financial center has shifted to New York. Due to the vast land, developed industry and commerce, and high consumption by a wealthy population in the United States, silk consumption has surged, and it has become the country with the highest raw silk consumption in the world. As Japanese silk focuses on sales to the United States, it has also risen to the top position of raw silk exporting countries. Chinese silk sales, on the other hand, have been dominated by France. In the French market, Japanese silk is not our enemy, while in the American market, Chinese silk is not to be taken lightly. Below is a table of raw silk imports by country in France over the past decade:

Table of Raw Silk Imports by Country in France Over the Years (Unit: 100 Bales)

From the above table, the position of Chinese silk in France is unparalleled by any country. No matter how fast Japan progresses, it still cannot compete with us. However, the rapid advancement of Japanese silk in the American market is something that we can only look up to.

Table of Raw Silk Consumption by Country in the United States Over the Past Decade (Unit: Bale)

Percentage Comparison Table of Raw Silk Consumption in the United States Over the Last Ten Years

From the above table, the expansion of Japanese silk's power in the American market has left almost no room for Chinese silk to exist. Under the condition that it is gradually being excluded from the American market, the urgent need to maintain its local market is an unchanging principle. (To be continued)
