Securities - Bond Market Fluctuates Up and Down for a Week 158

Last week, from October 19 to 24, the market situation of the Huashang Securities Exchange fluctuated quite a bit. The reason was that the current situation was unpredictable, sometimes tense and sometimes relaxed, and people's hearts were uneasy. Moreover, since this month's futures are approaching, swap trading was quite lively. How the future will unfold is still unpredictable. Looking back on last week, on Monday, the yarn and cotton market soared, slightly improving the stock market. On Tuesday, the environment was dull, and the public generally believed that peace could be declared, so major investors bought in, rising from one or two cents to six cents. On Wednesday, the five meetings between China and Japan were relatively smooth, continuing to rise from four cents to eight cents. On Thursday, due to extensive swap trading, rumors arose again, and selling pressure increased, falling back slightly from five cents to eight and a half cents. On Friday, there was still mostly swap trading, and the environment was still very dull, with market prices showing ups and downs. On Saturday, people's hearts were still not invigorated, and the situation was still impossible to predict. Major bullish investors exited, continuing to fall slightly from one cent to half a yuan. Today is the last day of this month's futures, and there may still be competition. As a result of the week's market prices, except for types A and B, which fell slightly by five cents and one cent respectively, all others rose by as much as one and a half cents. Yarn and Cotton - Prices of British and American Cotton Both Show Instability - Also True for Indian Cotton 159

Yesterday, when the American cotton market opened, the news from Liverpool was not good, so the bulls settled their positions and cotton farmers hedged their sales, causing the price of each month to fall by four to five pounds. Then, the advances from domestic and foreign peers were equal to the hedged sales amount, and it became slightly stable. Although observers said that the collections could reach 12 million bales, the public deeply believed that there were still discounts. The weather forecast was that the East had clouds, North Carolina had rain, and the Central and West were partly cloudy and partly sunny. At the close of the market, short positions were covered, with spot prices falling by three pounds and futures prices falling by three to seven pounds. British spot cotton fell by one point, and futures fell by five to six points. Indian cotton initially fell due to large-scale selling by futures traders, but then recovered due to short covering and retail buying. In total, Pingguer fell by 1.5 rupees, and Aomula and Bairoxi fell by 2 rupees. The original telegram recording is on the left (telegram of the 24th):

Spring and Autumn

Crab Thoughts 164

Now is the time when rice is ripe and crabs are fat, so large numbers of crawling generals are sent from elsewhere to Shanghai, displayed on the streets for people to view. Therefore, when we walk on the road, we are all struck by this group of swaggering crawling generals. However, crawl as you may, you will soon be served as a side dish, let's see how long you can crawl!

Crabs are also called "Intestineless Gentlemen." Yes, they have always crawled lawlessly, wanting more after getting something, truly liverless things! It's no wonder everyone wants to eat their flesh.

"Shrimp soldiers and crab generals," crabs are warriors in the water. However, they insist on coming ashore to swagger, so I give them a big name called "Marine Corps."

Crabs live in the water, but they insist on not being content with their lot and invade the land, not knowing that they have become a delicious treat for people and sacrificed their lives. Crabs, I advise you to be content and live your life in the water!

"Crawling" and "tyranny" are linked. Crabs are crawling generals, crawling from the water to the land. If it were to say that this crawling is "the kingly way," that would truly be shameless. Fortunately, crabs cannot speak, but those who can speak may be worse than even crabs?

Crab 165

— Wei Jing

Wearing a lined robe still doesn't provide enough warmth. At this time of year, the iron cages outside the cooked food shops on the streets of Shanghai begin to imprison the so-called "Yangcheng Lake hairy crabs." During this crab-eating season, gourmets hold wine glasses, laughing constantly. Vendors buy them in bulk, weighing them in units of twenty liang, and sell them by the catty, weighing them in units of thirteen liang and four qian. With a quick turnover, they only need to tie on a few strands of rice straw rope, and their pockets swell up like crab nets. Naturally, they can't help but beam with joy. As for the crab catchers, although they grope along the riverbank on dark, moonless nights, it's quite laborious, but with a little effort, they can easily catch baskets and hampers full of crabs, exchanging them for cash in the market to make a living. So, although crab catchers work hard, they usually have smiles on their faces during this crab-eating season. Laughter, laughter, laughter! Everyone is quite happy during this crab-eating season. The exception, the ones who should be shedding tears, I think, are the crabs that should be living happily in the water but are innocently caught, sold, and ultimately eaten, right?

Humans are, after all, smarter than crabs. Humans know that crabs are attracted to fire. Therefore, they often hang a lantern on the crab traps to lure the crabs to climb to the surface, waiting to be caught. After being caught, they are imprisoned in dark places to prevent the crabs from seeing the light and moving around. Because the more actively the crabs move after being removed from the water, the thinner they become. And when steaming them in a pot, their two claws and eight legs must be firmly bound to prevent them from making a final struggle at the bottom of the pot. According to gourmets, once a crab struggles at the bottom of the pot, the leg meat often becomes loose, and sometimes it is completely empty, greatly diminishing the flavor. Although the methods humans use on crabs are deceptive and cruel, who told them to hide a belly full of good stuff, arousing the appetites of gourmets when they see it? "A gentleman is innocent, but he is guilty of possessing treasure." I hold a similar view of the unfortunate crab.

"Famine of ropes, abundance of mosquitoes, cheap shrimp, chaotic crabs," is a popular saying among farmers in the Suzhou and Shanghai area, predicting the weather and human affairs. Several years ago, the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers overflowed, fulfilling the "famine of ropes" saying. This year, there are few ropes and many mosquitoes, indeed, a bountiful autumn harvest, demonstrating a remarkable omen. Before the Qi-Lu War, crabs were plentiful and cheap in the Suzhou and Shanghai area, with one yuan buying four catties of large crabs. Then, the war broke out. In the autumn before the January 28th Incident, the crab production in the Suzhou and Shanghai area was also very abundant, but soon after, turmoil occurred again. Although this is a coincidence, the saying of "chaotic crabs" cannot be denied as worth preserving. Therefore, I hope that from now on, crab production will decrease daily to avoid crab chaos. However, the gourmets of the world will surely consider my words a great damper and pray daily that my words will fortunately not come true.

Random Talk on Sharp and Rounded Sounds 166

— Yi Mei

The autumn scenery is gradually fading, and the purple crabs are becoming plump. Passing by the Five Clouds Sunrising Building, one sees everywhere the sideways-walking, armored knights, killed and cooked to satisfy human desires. I wonder if those in the world who daily engage in military expansion and aggression feel any fear or caution from this.

There are many kinds of crabs. Those from Yangcheng Lake and Taihu Lake are called lake crabs, filled with yellow fat, and are considered a delicacy. Fenhu Lake in Wujiang has purple pine crabs, which Lu You described in his poem as "round navels, piled high, Wujiang crabs." Tan Tang in Changshu has Tan Tang crabs, with soft shells and curled claws, also of high quality. Weizhou Village in Kunshan has Wei Chi crabs, rich in oil and overflowing with roe, with a flavor that is not inferior to lake crabs, but they are not as large.

Min Xi of Gui'an, styled Yanru, was fond of poetry and drinking, often sleeping drunk in taverns all day long, and often compared himself to the Minister of Personnel. He was good at painting crabs. Anyone who wanted him to paint would first have to offer him wine and food. He would paint from life after getting drunk, fully capturing their sharp and rounded forms. It is a pity that few of his surviving works have been passed down.

Shengtan stated: "Someone who excessively loved crabs was warned by others. He then made a vow, saying, 'I have a great wish, may I in my next life not be born where there are crabs, and may I not eat them.'" His words are curious and interesting, and perhaps Shengtan was talking about himself, which is unknown.

The large crabs that people call "zha crabs" should actually have "zha" written as "zha," meaning that they are eaten boiled in soup. The "Qing Jialu" has an entry about "zha crabs." "Zha" is pronounced zha. The pronunciation was mistakenly changed, and thus became "zha."

Lu Junshi E, who was skilled in medicine, said: "Any crab that has worms in its belly that look like small white stinkbugs should not be eaten, as eating it can easily cause wind disorders. Crabs are salty, cold, and slightly poisonous, and should not be eaten with zi or Jingjie. Crab roe can turn lacquer into water, so it is most effective for treating lacquer sores. It is said that burning crab claws can attract rats into the room, but I have never tried it. Buddhist books say that they wither and die after scattering their eggs. Food before the frost has poison, and after the frost, when they are about to hibernate, they taste delicious. The saying that they enter the sea is also nonsense."

There is a special way to eat crabs. Hang the crab on a rope, cut off half of its legs, so that they flex and extend automatically, and place a bowl underneath. The yellow and white will flow down from the tips of its legs. In less than an hour, the shell will be empty. The flowing yellow and white are mixed into chicken eggs and stewed to eat, the taste is fresh and unparalleled. But it is too cruel and inhumane, and benevolent people do not do it.

Among the delicacies, there are those who peel crab meat and crab roe and place them in crab shells, coat them with dry flour, and then fry them. I don't know what it's called. I think it should be called "crab shell yellow," which is very different from the oil-crisped and baked cakes sold on pancake stalls.

If you are poisoned from eating crab, and you suddenly don't know what medicine to use, you can quickly use orange peel with the pith removed, boil it into a soup, and drink it to detoxify. Also, crabs with eyes facing each other and spotted feet and red eyes should not be eaten. Also, cooked crabs have a bright red back shell, hence the poet's line, "In old autumn, there is no escape from a red back." However, if you cook the crabs with three to five zi stalks, they will turn blue.

Clear Crabs 168

— De Lin

These days, in the long streets and short alleys of Suzhou, one can often hear the cries of "clear crabs" for sale. The jade-like flesh and golden roe tempt the gourmets, and one cannot help but salivate. It reminds me of the late master of classical learning, Madam Tang Guoli, wife of Zhang Taiyan, who said: "If Yangcheng Lake crabs weren't so good, why would I live in Suzhou in this life?" It can be seen that the taste of crabs from Yangcheng Lake is truly moving!

Weiting, which is close to Suzhou, is known as the "land of fish and rice," and borders Clear Lake, which is especially famous for producing crabs. Therefore, as soon as the autumn wind rises, Weiting becomes a crab market. All the crabs are transported by train and ship to Beijing, Shanghai, and other places every day. However, the ones sold in the long streets and short alleys of Suzhou are directly from the countryside after being caught by farmers, so the prices are also lower. Therefore, in late autumn, anyone visiting Suzhou will buy Clear Crabs and return home to feast on them.

"When the rice ripens, the crabs are fat." During this rice-harvesting season, it is the time when "Clear Crabs" enter the market. Although "nine for females, ten for males," it is only past Mid-Autumn Festival, but because this year is not a leap year, it is already the season for chrysanthemums to bloom. Then, "round navels in September," this is the time! Gourmets can move their index fingers and hold their bowls.

The methods farmers use to catch crabs, in addition to setting nets, planting traps, and catching them by boat, the most common method is to plant poles in shallow water at dusk and hang lanterns on them. The gutless gentlemen who sink into the water see the light and come crawling, one after another. The farmers then spread mats on the ground, lie on the mats, and wait for the crabs to crawl over, and catch them with their hands. They are always successful. Those in the world who tend to be sycophantic, often falling into the net, are like these crabs!

There are different ways to eat crabs. I think the best way is to tie the eight legs and two claws of the crab with twine, put them in a steamer, and eat them while steaming, without letting them cool down. The taste is the most rich and delicious. If you boil them with water, you will inevitably lose the true taste. Crabs are cold in nature and have a fishy taste. After eating them, people in Suzhou are accustomed to drinking red sugar soup to relieve the cold, and then wash their hands with chrysanthemum leaves or white wine to remove the fishy taste.

Crab Tales 169

— Yan Yan

When boiling crabs, you must add a little perilla to test whether the crab is poisonous. If it is poisonous, the shell will definitely burst and cannot be eaten. It also has the effect of dispelling cold.

If you want to store and raise fresh crabs, you can use a jar, spread rice grains inside, put a layer of crabs on top, then spread another layer of rice grains, filling it layer by layer, and seal the mouth of the jar. Even after two or three months, they may not die, but once they are exposed to air, it will be completely ineffective. And after two or three months, the crabs will definitely be fatter than when they first entered the jar. Readers may want to try it.

When eating crabs, in addition to always serving with ginger vinegar and fine wine, you should also drink a cup of brown sugar water after eating, preferably with one or two slices of ginger in it, so as not to catch a cold and have a stomach ache.

Crabs and persimmons cannot be eaten together, as eating them will inevitably be fatal, causing excruciating abdominal pain. In addition, peanuts should not be eaten together either.

When boiling crabs, use cold water, and you must tie their claws and feet tightly with thin rope beforehand, otherwise they will easily fall off. The best way to eat crabs is not to boil them in water, but to tie the crabs and steam them on a rack in a pot. The taste is more delicious and palatable than boiling them in water. However, they must be washed clean.

To observe whether the crab's abdominal membrane is plump or thin, you can observe the phases of the moon. Crabs are always fattest during the dark moon and thinnest during the full moon.

When eating crabs, the fingers easily develop a crabby smell, which tastes very unpleasant. You can wash your hands with shochu and then scrub with soap and hot water to remove the crabby smell.

The above are all based on experience, so I dare to tell the readers.

The proofreaders did not change it, resulting in a mismatch with the topic of the special issue. We hereby declare this and apologize to the readers. (Juan)

All Kinds of Crabs 170

The festive season enters Double Ninth, holding a crab and cutting tender ginger. This is a crab poem sung by people in the past. Crabs are wonderful things, paired with reed wine and Xuan oranges, the flavor is excellent. Round navels in September, pointed in October, a seasonal fresh product, no wonder gourmets move their index fingers and feast on them.

Avoid using copper utensils to cook crabs, as eating them will definitely cause a chronic illness. Also, crabs with eyes facing each other, or spotted feet and red eyes, are all poisonous, and eating them can also kill people. Also, crabs are cold in nature and should not be eaten with persimmons or beer. According to a certain book, Shi Guogong wine and crabs eaten together can cause dysentery in mild cases and death in severe cases. Natural properties are incompatible, and you must know this.

According to crab catchers, the best crabs to choose are those with a green back, white belly, and red hair. It is also said that if you are poisoned from eating crab, quickly use orange peel with the pith removed, boil it into a soup, and drink it to detoxify. Another prescription is to mash fresh lotus root sections into a mud-like state and take it with hot wine.

Yunlin's Anecdotes contains a method for cooking crabs, saying to boil them with fresh ginger, perilla, orange peel, and salt. Once it comes to a boil, turn them over, and when it comes to a big boil, eat them. It is best to boil and eat the crabs one by one. At a rate of one person, you can boil two, eat them, and then boil more. Serve with mashed orange ginger vinegar.

Ancient people recorded special books about crabs, such as Gao Yisun's "Crab Treatise" of the Song Dynasty, Chuan Gong's "Crab Manual" of the Song Dynasty, and Lu Guimeng's "Crab Records" of the Tang Dynasty. It is a pity that they cannot be bought in bookstores, and one cannot quickly see them.

The various names of crabs, such as Gutless Gentleman and Sideways-Walking Armored Knight, are known to everyone. A more obscure one is Containing-Yellow Elder. "Qinglu" says: "Among the tastes of the four directions, Containing-Yellow Elder must be allowed to be the first," referring to crabs. It is also said: "Because he injured his tongue by eating a claw, he jokingly called crabs Tongue-Clipping Insects."

In zoological terms, crabs belong to the crustaceans among arthropods. The carapace of crabs is large, measuring more than a foot, and small, measuring like beans. In their larval stage, their shape is like shrimp. When they become adults, they shrink their tail segments and stick them to the cephalothorax, differentiating into pointed and rounded shapes by gender.

In China, the areas famous for producing crabs are Jiangxi and Zhejiang, such as the Mogang crabs of Haiyan, the Shiyan crabs of Yuyao, the Yangcheng Lake crabs of Kunshan, and the Jinzhao crabs of Yandang, all of which are well-known. As for this place, Shengfang Town in Wen'an County, Hebei, and Niuzhuang crabs are also very famous.

Crabs, when the frost falls and the oranges turn yellow and the tangerines turn green, the roe is full and the meat is fat and solid. The poems of the ancients have "Sending off guests with round crabs after the frost, orange slices fragrant yellow crabs are fat," which is clear evidence. (Teng Hua Xuan Master)

Pufferfish are prized in spring, purple crabs are plump in autumn, there is a time for everything. In the past, Sima Xiangru's articles imitated the behavior, and people compared him to a crab, and Wenjun finally ended her life, forbidding him to eat it. This matter is unusually beautiful and can strengthen conjugal love when heard. The scope of underdevelopment is quite broad, such as short stature, limb deformities, weak bones, congenital deficiencies, and small genitals. Usually, it mostly refers to the genitals, so the scope of discussion in this article is also mainly the genitals.

Acquired ones are more common than congenital ones. Supplement to the Shanghai Edition of Shen Bao

Talk

What Happens After the Jing and Wei Rivers Are Separated? 183

— Fang Kewen

On the 16th of this month, the Shanghai Guide Company, the "oldest store to start," had a notice saying: "Our company, in view of the needs of the times, first established the Shanghai Guide Company in mid-August of last year, hoping for the support of people from all walks of life in society in order to obtain satisfactory results. Unfortunately, people at the time misunderstood the true meaning of guidance, causing the emerging business to deteriorate day by day, which was not what our colleagues wished for. Therefore, we announced the closure of the business on the 15th of this month to show the separation of the Jing and Wei rivers..."

Looking at the advertisements posted by the Guide Company in the classified advertisements in the newspaper, those seductive and wonderful sentences saying that "misunderstanding the true meaning of guidance caused the emerging business to deteriorate day by day" is probably not a false accusation. Therefore, the principle of the Social Affairs Bureau to "properly formulate measures, those who aim for genuine guiding tours should be allowed to exist, otherwise they should be prohibited" feels very correct. "Those who aim for genuine guiding tours should be allowed to exist, otherwise they should be prohibited" is, of course, very correct and easy to say, but to identify "genuinely aiming for guiding tours" and "otherwise" is not as easy as writing a few words, not only not easy, but also very difficult. Moreover, even if the Jing and Wei rivers are separated, what measures should be taken?

The reason why it is very difficult is how to identify "genuinely aiming for guiding tours" and "operating an improper business in the name of guidance." Let's take a look at the predecessor of the Guide Company. As far as we know, most of the current Guide Companies have been transformed from previous dance schools, and the guides are mostly the dancers of the previous dance schools. Because the dance schools were banned, their lives told them that they could be guides, so they became guides. Once the Guide Company is banned again, then even if it is said that they will not be reduced to private prostitutes, their lives will tell them to do other things that are "operating an improper business in the name of ××."

So, let's take a step back and say that from now on, the guiding business is a pure "genuinely aiming for guiding tours," but what about those who are "generally prohibited"? If they want to survive, they probably still have to eat, they still have to wear clothes, and they still have to live in houses.

However, should we not "properly formulate measures" because of this? Of course not, this is cutting off food because of choking. However, if we think that treating the head when it hurts is a permanent solution, or wait for the feet to hurt before treating the feet, without trying to cure the root cause, this patient will die sooner or later.

I will just consider this as giving my loyal advice.

A Giant's Long Sleep 184

— Fangzi

Mr. Lu Xun:

On the lonely long road, you fought bitterly alone. In the end, just as you said, you were a stubborn ox, unwilling to let go of anything and fighting for every thing. You worked hard to cultivate forward until you stopped the last beat of your pulse. You taught us: we have to work; we young people have to work. Under the solemn banner of national revolution, we work down to earth, every drop counts.

In your life, there is only work. "You don't know what rest is, what entertainment is, work, work, you were still writing the day before you died..." — Mrs. Lu Xun's eulogy, we will work faithfully, and sacrifice for work.

We are locked in a room, without air, without light, the old etiquette, evil forces, and imperialism heavily surround us, invade us, and we are suffocating to death. But we are not willing to die docilely. We want to live! We want new life! We want to attack the dark bastions! Sir, on the eve of this storm, you stood up, went with us to charge, and resolutely led us to the front line.

But you — an old soldier is now in a long sleep.

"You are not dead," we all say you will not die. But your immortal soul will always live in the leaping hearts of every one of us young people. Your flesh and blood have fed us, and under the seeds you have sown, we will unleash a wave of rage of an era!

Although I have never met you, when I first saw you lying in the Universal Funeral Home, you were so familiar, like a long-lost teacher whom I have always admired. If it weren't for the solemn and tragic atmosphere around me invisibly stopping me, I could hardly help but shout affectionately: "Mr. Lu Xun!"

I glimpsed a set of stationery next to you. This set of stationery, ah, is your battleship, your cannonball, it has killed countless enemies. This sharp pen tip is a demon mirror, it mercilessly uncovers all the masks covering the surface, it is a goblin, return it as a goblin: it is a monster. Return it as a monster; it has inspired the thoughts of many people and motivated the spirits of many people.

The autumn sun accompanied the elegy, sorrow mixed with enthusiasm, countless students, workers, and writers, stars gathered together from all corners with feelings of mourning and respect and voluntarily came to the funeral.

"...He is the soul of our nation, he is the clarion call of the new era, calling on the masses to fight for survival! He resists imperialism, he resists the forces of darkness, his life is unyielding to the old age, and he has always worked for the revolution: our mentor" The lyrics followed the crowds in the procession, shaking.

Page 16

The coffin began to fall into the tomb. We paid our last and most respectful tribute to you, the giant who fought all your life. In the dim twilight, under the pale waning moon, a desolate song echoed in the tomb passage: "May you rest in peace, rest in peace!"

When will we stand in front of your grave and report to you that we have completed your will?

Stone Pen Painting (Continued) 185

— Zhifu

Xiao Ping used the stone pen to add a gun emplacement at the bottom, suggesting it had been destroyed by artillery fire.

Everyone laughed and said:

"We've won! We've won!" A group of people split into two factions, crawling on the ground and scribbling frantically with their stone pens...

"Hey! Let's all draw to our heart's content! You five draw airplanes, cannons, warships… we'll draw soldiers, these are our brave soldiers, resisting you! Look, how spirited they all are…"

Lu Xiaoping shouted as he drew, his body rolling in the dirt pile. His long gown was a mess, white in one place, black in another, completely unrecognizable.

"Okay! We have one, two, three… a total of six airplanes, five cannons. Let's fire!"

"Wait, wait!" Xu Shichang said, "Wait for my Second Battalion of soldiers to arrive before we start!"

What were the soldiers? They were simply the character "丁" (ding), with a head drawn on top, two feet drawn below, and a rifle slung over the shoulder!

After a while, both sides stopped. All that could be seen were white lines drawn all over the ground, but they regarded it as a vast battlefield.

"Xiaoping! Fire your rifles!"

"Alright! Let them fire!" He stumbled and rolled three or four feet, considering it an attack into the enemy's lines.

"Bang crash!"

You bang crash, he also bang crash, everyone bang bang crash crash...

Everyone was in a chaotic huddle, the ones drawing airplanes didn't have time to drop bombs, grabbing handfuls of dirt to throw, even using the stone pens in their hands as cannonballs. But Xiaoping and his group were truly brave, stepping forward to kick the airplanes, warships, and cannons to pieces. In the end, Ying Jinliang's side was considered defeated.

Xiaoping, Xu Shichang, and Lu Jiaju, wiping away the sweat on their foreheads, shouted, mouths and tongues racing:

"Firing requires everyone to have a sense of unity, unity is victory, let's all 'unite'!"

They returned to their ranks. The little lambs, still in the dim evening light, marched on with victorious steps, like a group of long-distance travelers, leaving this place in a grand manner.

Let's all sing a mountain song again!

"A small team of elementary school students, will mostly be talented adults in the future. We don't want to be slaves; we only want…"

The Pig Farmer 186

— Fei'er

The pig farmer raised pigs in the "Shamba" (1). Every day, he carried a shoulder pole to nearby shops and purchased leftover food from the "A Zongs" (2) at a low price—rice grains, vegetable scraps, fishy fish scales, and leftover meat slices… two big buckets full, carrying them back to feed the fat pigs, waiting for them to grow up to sell to people for slaughter.

That year, a swine fever epidemic broke out in the vicinity. Animals died one by one like flies encountering cold weather. One day they were fine, the next day they suddenly died. The government sent police to the countryside every day to inspect the burial of dead pigs. The pig farmers were in a panic. Every family in the "Shamba" was struck by disaster.

Chen Dadi said to Li Ahu:

"This is terrible! My wife and children are going to starve!"

Li Ahu replied, "Who isn't? So unlucky. I just brought my family from Tangshan last year, and this calamity strikes this year. Could it be that my wife is a jinx?"

But Ahu's heart was still calm. His pigs were not yet afflicted by the disaster, growing strong one by one: eating and sleeping well.

"May God bless us! Our family has always been kind and has never done anything evil." He prayed to the gods and comforted his anxious, gentle wife.

And the woman also went to the "Bógōng Temple" every day, asking for the protection of "Bógōng" (3).

"Great Bógōng! Protect our family. I love my husband, and I also love my four children. I have done no evil in this life. If I have not cultivated in my previous life, let me ask Bógōng to forgive me. I will slaughter a pig in the future to repay your divine grace."

The village became more and more panicked. Today the Xu family died a pig, tomorrow the A-San family died another pig. The most unfortunate was Chen Dadi, the entire pig herd died, leaving only two: a mother and a child.

The sound of crying spread from Chen's house to Li's house, making people feel sad. Ahu asked his wife:

"Did you go to worship Bógōng this morning?"

"Every day. Who dares to be disrespectful?"

Li Ahu felt relieved. He went to the market again to pick up leftovers. The pig slaughterer, the old Second Boss, said to him:

"Ahu, how many of your pigs are left? Are they sick? I need two pigs this afternoon, two."

Li Ahu proudly replied:

"Heh! Only other people's pigs will die out! Mine are fine, good pigs! But, let me tell you, the price must be higher. What good livestock is there this year?"

The Second Boss smiled slyly:

"Then, you can sell them to someone else. Don't be so rare, I would rather slaughter a few less every day. No one wants to do a loss-making business."

Li Ahu's stomach sank, feeling something was not right: what if those pigs also died? Who could guarantee anything this year?

So he frowned and changed his tune.

"Old Second Boss, let's talk it over. We're old customers, how could I take advantage of you like this? You can come and take them."

After filling his stomach with bread in the coffee shop, Li Ahu felt his idea was not bad. So, on the way home with the Old Second Boss, he talked about his family's good luck, practically beaming.

"It's really thanks to the blessing of the Great Bógōng that we have this good luck!" he said so gloriously.

But a few dozen steps away from home, he faintly heard what sounded like the crying of his wife and children. His heart sank, he frowned, but he still comforted himself: "Maybe it's someone else's family? Such a coincidence!" He rushed home in three steps instead of two.

As soon as he entered the door, he was so scared that his mouth opened wide. His wife, with disheveled hair, was crying and stomping her feet in front of the ancestors' shrine. The children surrounded her crying. He didn't say a word and ran to the pigsty. It was not good. Three stiff pig corpses were displayed in front of him. The pigpen had been sprayed with a lot of medicine by the authorities.

"It's over! It's over!" his heart cried. He ran into the house, forced a smile on the Old Second Boss, and said:

"It's okay, it's okay! You quickly take two of them away."

The Old Second Boss, seeing that the situation was bad, slyly lowered his face and said:

"I'm sorry, I don't dare to take them. The Mata (4) will fine me."

Then he left.

Li Ahu was stunned. A nameless anger suddenly rose from his heart. He grabbed his wife and gave her a heavy punch.

"You jinx! You…" he cursed.

There was another sharp wail from the livestock in the pigsty. Reporting that another pig had died.

(1) Villages in Southeast Asia.

(2) Cooks.

(3) The local deity worshiped by overseas Chinese.

(4) Colonial police.

Grandfather and Grandson 187

— Yu Yuyu

Ever since the doctor diagnosed me with early-stage tuberculosis, my family has been urging me to respect the doctor's advice and go for a walk in the park every morning. Persistently going to the park for a walk every morning is indeed the best way to maintain health, even for people without tuberculosis; however, I have a fixed amount of work to do every day, otherwise, our family's stomachs will all stop working. That eternal work has already made me feel very tired. Now, to add another task called "walking" outside of the scheduled time is truly more than I can "bear"! But my wife loves her husband, and my mother loves her son even more. Oppressed by these two great loves, I can only take a copy of the day's newspaper and go for a walk in the park. I always occupy a seat by the small pond, using this time to read some news. Normally, this task is done after dinner, but now it's moved forward twelve hours, perhaps that's the most direct benefit that walking gives me.

This has become a habit after several months. Because this added task is still quite relaxing, and it's just switching the time for reading the newspaper, although I have to leave the bed a little earlier every day, it's actually not much of a loss. As for what effect it has on the hygiene of the early-stage tuberculosis itself, no one can predict that.

There are many people who come to this park for a walk every day. They really come to walk, wandering back and forth. I often calculate how many circles some people have to make by the pond while reading the newspaper, or how many minutes it takes a pair of lovers, like Westerners, to walk across a piece of grass. The ones like me who sit by the pond from the time they come in until they leave are the grandfather and grandson in the title, but this relationship is also what I speculate, maybe it's a son, too.

Now let's assume it's the relationship between grandfather and grandson. The grandfather's age is at least in his late fifties, with a head of long, silvery-gray hair. If he were in a Western oil painting, he would definitely be a great poet. But he is dressed in worn-out clothes, not because he is sloppy, but the holes on the corners of his robe are neatly patched with cloth of the same color. At most, you can only say he is a thrifty old man. The grandson is about seven or eight years old, much more beautiful than his grandfather. In summer, he wears linen overalls, and now he wears wool shirts and trousers. In a few days, I guess he will definitely have a beautiful coat.

They arrive at the park around the same time as me, but I always leave first. Didn't I say that there is a fixed time for work every day? They always come to sit by the pond, too. The grandfather sits on the chair, and the grandson sits on the grass. Then they start their breakfast, which is a bag of biscuits and a piece of bread. The biscuits are for the grandson, and the old man chews on the hard bread. Afterwards, the grandson rolls back and forth on the grass, never stopping for a moment. The grandfather is like a Bodhisattva enshrined in a Buddhist niche, closing his eyes to rest. Occasionally, he opens his eyelids and only glances at the grandson on the grass before closing them again.

When autumn came, they didn't come to the park for a few days. When I met them again a day later, the old man's spirit was even more decadent. He didn't eat bread either, just fell asleep on the grass, letting his grandson splash water by the pond. The sound of bamboo sticks hitting the water surface was "crackle crackle". He pretended not to hear it—perhaps he was really preoccupied with other thoughts.

So I also started to "think." Maybe the old man also has a fixed time to do work every day. That eternal work will make him even more tired than me, but he loves his grandson, so he added this "walking" task. He is naturally more than he can "bear." Closing his eyes every day is probably to prepare for the energy he will spend on the scheduled work…

This guess is unfounded and almost a fantasy. But my thoughts have been limited by that circle. I start from this starting point every day to speculate on the more distant future. I hope the old man lives a long life, hoping that he will continue to greedily chew on a hard piece of bread every day.

Humans are connected by a great love, grandfather to grandson, mother to son, wife to husband… Under the oppression of this great love, everyone's life is determined.

The daily walk will probably continue as long as the scheduled work, because I dare not ask the doctor who diagnosed me what stage my early-stage tuberculosis has progressed to (naturally hoping it has become better).

Professor Shan Ci-gang of Yongjia is a famous expert in epigraphy and archaeology. His calligraphy encompasses running script, cursive script, seal script, and official script. His works have long been esteemed both at home and abroad. To the left is a large seal script text by him, which reads, "Maintaining a high position with caution is like crossing deep water" and "Loving antiquity and taking pleasure in the Way does not preclude minor streams."

Movies

Tianyi Magazine 193

"By the Huangpu River" is a drama written about the local scenery of Shanghai. It has now been edited. It has been test-screened once. The actors' performances, recording, and photography all have special achievements.

Tao Jin plays a young man in "Yangliu Village". It is another tough performance, which is similar to the rickshaw puller in "By the Huangpu River" in different ways.

Little Star Li Songyun appeared on camera in "Yangliu Village".

Tang Jie has recovered from his foot injury and went to the company today to film "Yangliu Village".

Wen Yimin's "Female Student" script has been approved and is being rehearsed diligently every day and will soon begin filming.

After more than a month of hard work, Zuo Ming has completed the re-examination script of "Mr. Wang's Way of Making Money" and sent it to Beijing for review today.

Fan Xuepeng has not filmed for more than a year since "Mother". Recently, she performed in "Yangliu Village", playing a pure woman of the new era.

Tianyi Company specially recommends newcomers Chen Qixia, Tao Jin and Leng Bo. Their acting skills in "By the Huangpu River" are very exquisite. Seeing the same old faces on the Chinese silver screen is really a bit annoying, so Tianyi's efforts to recommend newcomers this time is indeed a pleasing thing.

"Night Meeting" scene Xie Jun and Yuan Shaomei

A Bundle of Telecommunications 194

In the era of silent films, the film "Ramona" starring Doris Deleio once caused a sensation far and wide. Now, 20th Century Fox has made the story into a sound film, with Loretta Young playing the role of Ramona. The film is all in color, making it even more beautiful and lovely. It is said that the film has arrived in Shanghai and will soon be released at the Daguang Cinema.

Anyone who has seen Guotai's recently released "Spring Fatigue by the Green Window" cannot help but praise the new star Simone Simon extremely. Her new work after "Green Window Spring Fatigue" is Ladies in Love, which at first glance is another film describing women's love, and co-starring with her are Jenny Gaynor, Loretta Young and Constance Bennett.

The war epic "The Story of Louis Pasteur", starring Frederic March, Warner Baxter, and Leon Rimaux, has been playing to full houses since it was simultaneously released in the Da Guangming and Guotai theaters. It is said that it is indeed one of the best works among the war films in recent years.

Tan Ying and Zhao Dan have achieved amazing success in their acting in "Little Lingzi". The most lovely thing about the film is that the dialogue is witty and the performance is relaxed, with a great Western film flavor. Therefore, all friends who have seen "Little Lingzi" at Jincheng are very satisfied and unanimously praised it as a masterpiece of domestic films.
